      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">
        Culture
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hispanic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Culture">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Miguel_de_Cervantes_Prize" title="Miguel de Cervantes Prize">
        Miguel de Cervantes Prize
       </a>
       is awarded to Hispanic writers, whereas the
       <a href="/wiki/Latin_Grammy_Award" title="Latin Grammy Award">
        Latin Grammy Award
       </a>
       recognizes Hispanic and Portuguese musicians, and the Platino Awards as given to outstanding Hispanic films.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Music">
        Music
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hispanic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Music">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main articles:
       <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Spain" title="Music of Spain">
        Music of Spain
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispanic_music" title="Hispanic music">
        Hispanic music
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_music_(genre)" title="Latin music (genre)">
        Latin music (genre)
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Folk and popular dance and music also varies greatly among Hispanics. For instance, the music from Spain is a lot different from the
       <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_America" title="Hispanic America">
        Hispanic American
       </a>
       , although there is a high grade of exchange between both continents. In addition, due to the high national development of the diverse
       <a href="/wiki/Nationalities_and_regions_of_Spain" title="Nationalities and regions of Spain">
        nationalities and regions of Spain
       </a>
       , there is a lot of music in the
       <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_Spain" title="Languages of Spain">
        different languages of the Peninsula
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Catalan_language" title="Catalan language">
        Catalan
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Galician_language" title="Galician language">
        Galician
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Basque_language" title="Basque language">
        Basque
       </a>
       , mainly). See, for instance,
       <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Catalonia" title="Music of Catalonia">
        Music of Catalonia
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Rock_catal%C3%A0" title="Rock català">
        Rock català
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Galicia,_Cantabria_and_Asturias" title="Music of Galicia, Cantabria and Asturias">
        Music of Galicia, Cantabria and Asturias
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Basque_music" title="Basque music">
        Basque music
       </a>
       .
       <a href="/wiki/Flamenco" title="Flamenco">
        Flamenco
       </a>
       is also a very popular music style in Spain, especially in
       <a href="/wiki/Andalusia" title="Andalusia">
        Andalusia
       </a>
       . Spanish ballads "romances" can be traced in Argentina as "milongas", same structure but different scenarios.
      </p>
      <p>
       On the other side of the ocean, Hispanic America is also home to a wide variety of music, even though "Latin" music is often erroneously thought of, as a single genre. Hispanic Caribbean music tends to favor complex polyrhythms of African origin.
       <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Mexico" title="Music of Mexico">
        Mexican music
       </a>
       shows combined influences of mostly European and Native American origin, while traditional Northern Mexican music —
       <a href="/wiki/Norte%C3%B1o_(music)" title="Norteño (music)">
        norteño
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Banda_music" title="Banda music">
        banda
       </a>
       —
       <a href="/wiki/Polka" title="Polka">
        polka
       </a>
       , has influence from polka music brought by
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Europe" title="Central Europe">
        Central European
       </a>
       settlers to
       <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">
        Mexico
       </a>
       which later influenced western music. The music of Hispanic Americans — such as
       <a href="/wiki/Tejano_music" title="Tejano music">
        tejano music
       </a>
       — has influences in
       <a href="/wiki/Rock_music" title="Rock music">
        rock
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">
        jazz
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Rhythm_and_blues" title="Rhythm and blues">
        R&amp;B
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Latin_pop" title="Latin pop">
        pop
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Country_music" title="Country music">
        country music
       </a>
       as well as traditional Mexican music such as
       <a href="/wiki/Mariachi" title="Mariachi">
        Mariachi
       </a>
       . Meanwhile, native
       <a href="/wiki/Andes" title="Andes">
        Andean
       </a>
       sounds and melodies are the backbone of Peruvian and Bolivian music, but also play a significant role in the popular music of most South American countries and are heavily incorporated into the folk music of Ecuador and Chile and the tunes of Colombia, and again in Chile where they play a fundamental role in the form of the greatly followed
       <a href="/wiki/Nueva_canci%C3%B3n" title="Nueva canción">
        nueva canción
       </a>
       . In U.S. communities of immigrants from these countries it is common to hear these styles.
       <a href="/wiki/Latin_pop" title="Latin pop">
        Latin pop
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Rock_en_Espa%C3%B1ol" title="Rock en Español">
        Rock en Español
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hip-hop" title="Hip-hop">
        Latin hip-hop
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Salsa_(dance)" title="Salsa (dance)">
        Salsa
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Merengue_(dance)" title="Merengue (dance)">
        Merengue
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Colombian_cumbia&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Colombian cumbia (page does not exist)">
        colombian cumbia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Reggaeton" title="Reggaeton">
        Reggaeton
       </a>
       styles tend to appeal to the broader Hispanic population, and varieties of Cuban music are popular with many Hispanics of all backgrounds.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">
        Literature
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hispanic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Literature">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hispanic_literature" title="Hispanic literature">
        Hispanic literature
       </a>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:182px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Medal_of_the_Miguel_de_Cervantes_Prize.svg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="502" data-file-width="441" height="205" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Medal_of_the_Miguel_de_Cervantes_Prize.svg/180px-Medal_of_the_Miguel_de_Cervantes_Prize.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Medal_of_the_Miguel_de_Cervantes_Prize.svg/270px-Medal_of_the_Miguel_de_Cervantes_Prize.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Medal_of_the_Miguel_de_Cervantes_Prize.svg/360px-Medal_of_the_Miguel_de_Cervantes_Prize.svg.png 2x" width="180"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Medal_of_the_Miguel_de_Cervantes_Prize.svg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         <a href="/wiki/Miguel_de_Cervantes_Prize" title="Miguel de Cervantes Prize">
          Miguel de Cervantes Prize
         </a>
         , most prestigious literary award in the Spanish language
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Spanish-language literature and folklore is very rich and is influenced by a variety of countries. There are thousands of writers from many places, and dating from the Middle Ages to the present. Some of the most recognized writers are
       <a href="/wiki/Miguel_de_Cervantes" title="Miguel de Cervantes">
        Miguel de Cervantes Saavedra
       </a>
       (Spain),
       <a href="/wiki/Lope_de_Vega" title="Lope de Vega">
        Lope de Vega
       </a>
       (Spain),
       <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Calder%C3%B3n_de_la_Barca" title="Pedro Calderón de la Barca">
        Calderón de la Barca
       </a>
       (Spain),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jose_Rizal" title="Jose Rizal">
        Jose Rizal
       </a>
       (Philippines),
       <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Fuentes" title="Carlos Fuentes">
        Carlos Fuentes
       </a>
       (Mexico),
       <a href="/wiki/Octavio_Paz" title="Octavio Paz">
        Octavio Paz
       </a>
       (Mexico),
       <a href="/wiki/Miguel_%C3%81ngel_Asturias" title="Miguel Ángel Asturias">
        Miguel Ángel Asturias
       </a>
       (Guatemala),
       <a href="/wiki/George_Santayana" title="George Santayana">
        George Santayana
       </a>
       (US),
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mart%C3%AD" title="José Martí">
        José Martí
       </a>
       (Cuba),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sabine_Ulibarri" title="Sabine Ulibarri">
        Sabine Ulibarri
       </a>
       (US),
       <a href="/wiki/Federico_Garc%C3%ADa_Lorca" title="Federico García Lorca">
        Federico García Lorca
       </a>
       (Spain),
       <a href="/wiki/Miguel_de_Unamuno" title="Miguel de Unamuno">
        Miguel de Unamuno
       </a>
       (Spain),
       <a href="/wiki/Gabriel_Garc%C3%ADa_M%C3%A1rquez" title="Gabriel García Márquez">
        Gabriel García Márquez
       </a>
       (Colombia),
       <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Pombo" title="Rafael Pombo">
        Rafael Pombo
       </a>
       (Colombia),
       <a href="/wiki/Horacio_Quiroga" title="Horacio Quiroga">
        Horacio Quiroga
       </a>
       (Uruguay),
       <a href="/wiki/R%C3%B3mulo_Gallegos" title="Rómulo Gallegos">
        Rómulo Gallegos
       </a>
       (Venezuela),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Luis_Rodriguez_Varela" title="Luis Rodriguez Varela">
        Luis Rodriguez Varela
       </a>
       (Philippines),
       <a href="/wiki/Rub%C3%A9n_Dar%C3%ADo" title="Rubén Darío">
        Rubén Darío
       </a>
       (Nicaragua),
       <a href="/wiki/Mario_Vargas_Llosa" title="Mario Vargas Llosa">
        Mario Vargas Llosa
       </a>
       (Peru),
       <a href="/wiki/Giannina_Braschi" title="Giannina Braschi">
        Giannina Braschi
       </a>
       (Puerto Rico),
       <a href="/wiki/Cristina_Peri_Rossi" title="Cristina Peri Rossi">
        Cristina Peri Rossi
       </a>
       (Uruguay),
       <a href="/wiki/Luisa_Valenzuela" title="Luisa Valenzuela">
        Luisa Valenzuela
       </a>
       (Argentina),
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Roberto_Quesada&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Roberto Quesada (page does not exist)">
        Roberto Quesada
       </a>
       (Honduras),
       <a href="/wiki/Julio_Cort%C3%A1zar" title="Julio Cortázar">
        Julio Cortázar
       </a>
       (Argentina),
       <a href="/wiki/Pablo_Neruda" title="Pablo Neruda">
        Pablo Neruda
       </a>
       (Chile),
       <a href="/wiki/Gabriela_Mistral" title="Gabriela Mistral">
        Gabriela Mistral
       </a>
       (Chile),
       <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Luis_Borges" title="Jorge Luis Borges">
        Jorge Luis Borges
       </a>
       (Argentina),
       <a href="/wiki/Pedro_Henr%C3%ADquez_Ure%C3%B1a" title="Pedro Henríquez Ureña">
        Pedro Henríquez Ureña
       </a>
       (Dominican Republic),
       <a href="/wiki/Ernesto_Sabato" title="Ernesto Sabato">
        Ernesto Sabato
       </a>
       (Argentina),
       <a href="/wiki/Juan_Tom%C3%A1s_%C3%81vila_Laurel" title="Juan Tomás Ávila Laurel">
        Juan Tomás Ávila Laurel
       </a>
       (Equatorial Guinea),
       <a href="/wiki/Ciro_Alegr%C3%ADa" title="Ciro Alegría">
        Ciro Alegría
       </a>
       (Peru),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joaquin_Garcia_Monge" title="Joaquin Garcia Monge">
        Joaquin Garcia Monge
       </a>
       (Costa Rica), and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jesus_Balmori" title="Jesus Balmori">
        Jesus Balmori
       </a>
       (Philippines).
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">
        Sports
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hispanic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Sports">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       In the majority of the Hispanic countries,
       <a href="/wiki/Association_football" title="Association football">
        association football
       </a>
       is the most popular sport. The men's national teams of Argentine, Uruguay and Spain have won the
       <a href="/wiki/FIFA_World_Cup" title="FIFA World Cup">
        FIFA World Cup
       </a>
       a total five times. The Spanish
       <a href="/wiki/La_Liga" title="La Liga">
        La Liga
       </a>
       is one of the most popular in the world, known for
       <a href="/wiki/FC_Barcelona" title="FC Barcelona">
        FC Barcelona
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Real_Madrid" title="Real Madrid">
        Real Madrid
       </a>
       . Meanwhile, the
       <a href="/wiki/Argentine_Primera_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="Argentine Primera División">
        Argentine Primera División
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mexican_Primera_Divisi%C3%B3n" title="Mexican Primera División">
        Mexican Primera División
       </a>
       are two of the strongest leagues in the Americas.
      </p>
      <p>
       However,
       <a href="/wiki/Baseball" title="Baseball">
        baseball
       </a>
       is the most popular sport in some Central American and Caribbean countries (especially Cuba, Dominican Republic, Puerto Rico and Venezuela), as well as in the diaspora in the United States. Notable Hispanic teams in early baseball are the
       <a href="/wiki/All_Cubans" title="All Cubans">
        All Cubans
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cuban_Stars_(West)" title="Cuban Stars (West)">
        Cuban Stars
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/New_York_Cubans" title="New York Cubans">
        New York Cubans
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Hispanic_Heritage_Baseball_Museum" title="Hispanic Heritage Baseball Museum">
        Hispanic Heritage Baseball Museum
       </a>
       recognizes Hispanic baseball personalities. Nearly 30 percent (22 percent foreign-born Latinos) of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MLB" title="MLB">
        MLB
       </a>
       players today have Hispanic heritage.
      </p>
      <p>
       Several Hispanic sportspeople have been successful worldwide, such as
       <a href="/wiki/Diego_Maradona" title="Diego Maradona">
        Diego Maradona
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alfredo_di_Stefano" title="Alfredo di Stefano">
        Alfredo di Stefano
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Messi" title="Lionel Messi">
        Lionel Messi
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Diego_Forl%C3%A1n" title="Diego Forlán">
        Diego Forlán
       </a>
       (association football),
       <a href="/wiki/Juan_Manuel_Fangio" title="Juan Manuel Fangio">
        Juan Manuel Fangio
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Juan_Pablo_Montoya" title="Juan Pablo Montoya">
        Juan Pablo Montoya
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Eliseo_Salazar" title="Eliseo Salazar">
        Eliseo Salazar
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Fernando_Alonso" title="Fernando Alonso">
        Fernando Alonso
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Marc_Gen%C3%A9" title="Marc Gené">
        Marc Gené
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Sainz" title="Carlos Sainz">
        Carlos Sainz
       </a>
       (auto racing),
       <a href="/wiki/%C3%81ngel_Nieto" title="Ángel Nieto">
        Ángel Nieto
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Dani_Pedrosa" title="Dani Pedrosa">
        Dani Pedrosa
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Lorenzo" title="Jorge Lorenzo">
        Jorge Lorenzo
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Marc_M%C3%A1rquez" title="Marc Márquez">
        Marc Márquez
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Marc_Coma" title="Marc Coma">
        Marc Coma
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Nani_Roma" title="Nani Roma">
        Nani Roma
       </a>
       (motorcycle racing),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emanuel_Gin%C3%B3bili" title="Emanuel Ginóbili">
        Emanuel Ginóbili
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pau_Gasol" title="Pau Gasol">
        Pau Gasol
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Marc_Gasol" title="Marc Gasol">
        Marc Gasol
       </a>
       (basketball),
       <a href="/wiki/Julio_C%C3%A9sar_Ch%C3%A1vez" title="Julio César Chávez">
        Julio César Chávez
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sa%C3%BAl_%C3%81lvarez" title="Saúl Álvarez">
        Saúl Álvarez
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Carlos_Monz%C3%B3n" title="Carlos Monzón">
        Carlos Monzón
       </a>
       (boxing),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Miguel_Indurain" title="Miguel Indurain">
        Miguel Indurain
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Alberto_Contador" title="Alberto Contador">
        Alberto Contador
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Santiago_Botero" title="Santiago Botero">
        Santiago Botero
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Rigoberto_Ur%C3%A1n" title="Rigoberto Urán">
        Rigoberto Urán
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Nairo_Quintana" title="Nairo Quintana">
        Nairo Quintana
       </a>
       (cycling),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roberto_de_Vicenzo" title="Roberto de Vicenzo">
        Roberto de Vicenzo
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/%C3%81ngel_Cabrera" title="Ángel Cabrera">
        Ángel Cabrera
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Sergio_Garc%C3%ADa" title="Sergio García">
        Sergio García
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Severiano_Ballesteros" title="Severiano Ballesteros">
        Severiano Ballesteros
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Jos%C3%A9_Mar%C3%ADa_Olaz%C3%A1bal" title="José María Olazábal">
        José María Olazábal
       </a>
       (golf),
       <a href="/wiki/Luciana_Aymar" title="Luciana Aymar">
        Luciana Aymar
       </a>
       (field hockey),
       <a href="/wiki/Rafael_Nadal" title="Rafael Nadal">
        Rafael Nadal
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Marcelo_R%C3%ADos" title="Marcelo Ríos">
        Marcelo Ríos
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Guillermo_Vilas" title="Guillermo Vilas">
        Guillermo Vilas
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Gabriela_Sabatini" title="Gabriela Sabatini">
        Gabriela Sabatini
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Juan_Mart%C3%ADn_del_Potro" title="Juan Martín del Potro">
        Juan Martín del Potro
       </a>
       (tennis).
      </p>
      <p>
       Notable Hispanic sports television networks are
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ESPN_Latin_America" title="ESPN Latin America">
        ESPN Latin America
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fox_Sports_Latin_America" title="Fox Sports Latin America">
        Fox Sports Latin America
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/TyC_Sports" title="TyC Sports">
        TyC Sports
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">
        Religion
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hispanic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Religion">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       With regard to religious affiliation among Spanish-speakers,
       <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">
        Christianity
       </a>
       — specifically
       <a href="/wiki/Catholic_Church" title="Catholic Church">
        Roman Catholicism
       </a>
       — is usually the first religious tradition that comes to mind
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (September 2014)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       . The Spaniards and the Portuguese took the Roman Catholic faith to Ibero-America and the Philippines, and Roman Catholicism remains the predominant religion amongst most Hispanics. A small but growing number of Hispanics belong to a
       <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">
        Protestant
       </a>
       denomination.
      </p>
      <table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content" role="presentation">
       <tr>
        <td class="mbox-image">
         <div style="width:52px">
          <img alt="Unbalanced scales.svg" data-file-height="354" data-file-width="400" height="40" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/45px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/68px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/Unbalanced_scales.svg/90px-Unbalanced_scales.svg.png 2x" width="45"/>
         </div>
        </td>
        <td class="mbox-text">
         <div class="mbox-text-span">
          <b>
           This section's representation of one or more viewpoints about a controversial issue may be unbalanced or inaccurate.
          </b>
          <span class="hide-when-compact">
           Please
           <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Hispanic&amp;action=edit">
            improve the article
           </a>
           or discuss the issue on the
           <a href="/wiki/Talk:Hispanic" title="Talk:Hispanic">
            talk page
           </a>
           .
          </span>
          <small>
           <i>
            (December 2009)
           </i>
          </small>
         </div>
        </td>
       </tr>
      </table>
      <p>
       There are also Spanish-speaking
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jew" title="Jew">
        Jews
       </a>
       , most of whom are the descendants of
       <a href="/wiki/Ashkenazi_Jews" title="Ashkenazi Jews">
        Ashkenazi Jews
       </a>
       who migrated from Europe (German Jews, Russian Jews, Polish Jews, etc.) to Hispanic America, particularly
       <a href="/wiki/Argentina" title="Argentina">
        Argentina
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Uruguay" title="Uruguay">
        Uruguay
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Peru" title="Peru">
        Peru
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">
        Cuba
       </a>
       (Argentina is host to the third largest Jewish population in the Western Hemisphere, after the United States and Canada)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
        <a href="#cite_note-92">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
        <a href="#cite_note-93">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
       in the 19th century and following World War II. Many Spanish-speaking Jews also originate from the small communities of reconverted descendants of
       <a href="/wiki/Anusim" title="Anusim">
        anusim
       </a>
       — those whose Spanish
       <a href="/wiki/Sephardi_Jews" title="Sephardi Jews">
        Sephardi Jewish
       </a>
       ancestors long ago hid their Jewish ancestry and beliefs in fear of persecution by the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Inquisition" title="Spanish Inquisition">
        Spanish Inquisition
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">
        Iberian Peninsula
       </a>
       and Ibero-America. The Spanish Inquisition led to a large number of forced conversions of Spanish Jews.
      </p>
      <p>
       Genetic studies on the (male)
       <a href="/wiki/Y_chromosome" title="Y chromosome">
        Y-chromosome
       </a>
       conducted by the
       <a href="/wiki/University_of_Leeds" title="University of Leeds">
        University of Leeds
       </a>
       in 2008 appear to support the idea that the number of forced conversions have been previously underestimated significantly. They found that twenty percent of Spanish males have Y-chromosomes associated with Sephardic Jewish ancestry.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
        <a href="#cite_note-94">
         [94]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This may imply that there were more forced conversions than was previously thought.
      </p>
      <p>
       There are also thought to be many Catholic-professing descendants of
       <a href="/wiki/Marrano" title="Marrano">
        marranos
       </a>
       and Spanish-speaking
       <a href="/wiki/Crypto-Judaism" title="Crypto-Judaism">
        crypto-Jews
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Southwestern_United_States" title="Southwestern United States">
        Southwestern United States
       </a>
       and scattered through Hispanic America. Additionally, there are Sephardic Jews who are descendants of those Jews who fled Spain to Turkey,
       <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">
        Syria
       </a>
       , and North Africa, some of whom have now migrated to Hispanic America, holding on to some Spanish/Sephardic customs, such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Judaeo-Spanish" title="Judaeo-Spanish">
        Ladino
       </a>
       language, which mixes Spanish, Hebrew, Arabic and others, though written with Hebrew and Latin characters.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95">
        <a href="#cite_note-95">
         [95]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">
        Ladinos
       </a>
       were also African slaves captive in Spain held prior to the colonial period in the Americas. (See also
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_the_Jews_in_Latin_America" title="History of the Jews in Latin America">
        History of the Jews in Hispanic America
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_Latin_American_Jews" title="List of Latin American Jews">
        List of Hispanic American Jews
       </a>
       .)
      </p>
      <p>
       Among the Spanish-speaking Catholics, most communities celebrate their homeland's
       <a href="/wiki/Patron_saint" title="Patron saint">
        patron saint
       </a>
       , dedicating a day for this purpose with festivals and religious services. Some Spanish-speakers syncretize Roman Catholicism and African or Native American rituals and beliefs. Such is the case of
       <a href="/wiki/Santer%C3%ADa" title="Santería">
        Santería
       </a>
       , popular with
       <a href="/wiki/Afro-Cuban" title="Afro-Cuban">
        Afro-Cubans
       </a>
       , which combines old African beliefs in the form of Roman Catholic saints and rituals. Other syncretistic beliefs include
       <a href="/wiki/Spiritism" title="Spiritism">
        Spiritism
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Curandero" title="Curandero">
        Curanderismo
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       While a tiny minority, there are some Muslims in Latin America, in the US, and in the Philippines. Those in the Philippines live predominantly in the province forming the
       <a href="/wiki/Autonomous_Region_in_Muslim_Mindanao" title="Autonomous Region in Muslim Mindanao">
        Autonomous Region in Muslim Mindanao
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       In the United States, some 65% of Hispanics and Latinos report themselves Catholic and 21% Protestant, with 13% having no affiliation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
        <a href="#cite_note-96">
         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A minority among the Roman Catholics, about one in five, are
       <a href="/wiki/Charismatic_Christianity" title="Charismatic Christianity">
        charismatics
       </a>
       . Among the Protestant, 85% are "
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Born_again_(Christianity)" title="Born again (Christianity)">
        Born-again Christians
       </a>
       " and belong to
       <a href="/wiki/Evangelicalism" title="Evangelicalism">
        Evangelical
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Pentecostalism" title="Pentecostalism">
        Pentecostal
       </a>
       churches. Among the smallest groups, less than 4%, are Jewish.
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Cultural_heritage_according_to_UNESCO">
        Cultural heritage according to UNESCO
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hispanic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Cultural heritage according to UNESCO">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <p>
       The Hispanic world, according to the United Nations World Heritage Committee, has contributed substantially more than any other ethnicity to the cultural heritage of the world. A World Heritage Cultural Site is a place such as a building, city, complex, or monument that is listed by the United Nations Educational, Scientific and Cultural Organization (UNESCO) as being of special cultural significance. Of a total of 802 Cultural World Heritage Sites recognized by the United Nations as of July 2015, 114 are located in Hispanic countries. Spain alone has 39 cultural sites, only second in the world to Italy.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2017)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">
        See also

       <span class="mw-editsection">

        </a>

        </span>
       </span>

      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">
        Notes
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Hispanic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Notes">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
